	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Manchester Piccadilly station</h1>

<p><b>Manchester Piccadilly</b> is the principal railway station in <a href="/wiki/Manchester" title="Manchester">Manchester</a>, England. Opened as <b>Store Street</b> in 1842, it was renamed <b>Manchester London Road</b> in 1847 and Manchester Piccadilly in 1960. Located to the south-east of <a href="/wiki/Manchester_city_centre" title="Manchester city centre">Manchester city centre</a>, it hosts long-distance intercity and cross-country services to national destinations including <a href="/wiki/Euston_railway_station" title="Euston railway station">London</a>, <a href="/wiki/Birmingham_New_Street_railway_station" title="Birmingham New Street railway station">Birmingham</a>, <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Central_station" title="Glasgow Central station">Glasgow</a>, <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh_Waverley_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Edinburgh Waverley station">Edinburgh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cardiff_Central_railway_station" title="Cardiff Central railway station">Cardiff</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bristol_Temple_Meads_railway_station" title="Bristol Temple Meads railway station">Bristol</a>, <a href="/wiki/Exeter_St_Davids_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Exeter St Davids railway station">Exeter</a>, <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_railway_station" title="Plymouth railway station">Plymouth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Reading_railway_station" title="Reading railway station">Reading</a>, <a href="/wiki/Southampton_Central_railway_station" title="Southampton Central railway station">Southampton</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Bournemouth_railway_station" title="Bournemouth railway station">Bournemouth</a>; regional services to destinations in <a href="/wiki/Northern_England" title="Northern England">Northern England</a> including <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_Lime_Street_railway_station" title="Liverpool Lime Street railway station">Liverpool</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leeds_railway_station" title="Leeds railway station">Leeds</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Sheffield railway station">Sheffield</a>, <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_railway_station" title="Newcastle railway station">Newcastle</a> and <a href="/wiki/York_railway_station" title="York railway station">York</a>; and local commuter services around <a href="/wiki/Greater_Manchester" title="Greater Manchester">Greater Manchester</a>. It is one of 19 major stations managed by <a href="/wiki/Network_Rail" title="Network Rail">Network Rail</a>. The station has 14 platforms, twelve terminal and two through platforms. Piccadilly is also a major interchange with the <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Metrolink" title="Manchester Metrolink">Metrolink</a> light rail system with two <a href="#Piccadilly_tram_stop">tram platforms</a> in its <a href="/wiki/Undercroft" title="Undercroft">undercroft</a>.
</p><p>Piccadilly is the busiest station in the <a href="/wiki/Manchester_station_group" title="Manchester station group">Manchester station group</a> with nearly 28 million passenger entries and exits between April 2017 and March 2018, (the other major stations in Manchester are <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Oxford_Road_railway_station" title="Manchester Oxford Road railway station">Oxford Road</a> and <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Victoria_station" title="Manchester Victoria station">Victoria</a>). It is the fourth busiest station in the United Kingdom outside London.<sup id="cite_ref-ORR-2013_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ORR-2013-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> The station hosts services from six train operating companies. It is the second busiest <a href="/wiki/Interchange_station" title="Interchange station">interchange station</a> outside London, with almost 3.8&#160;million passengers changing trains annually.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> 
</p><p>Between the late 1990s and early 2000s, Piccadilly Station was refurbished, taking five years and costing £100 million (in 2002), it was the most expensive improvement on the UK rail network at the time.<sup id="cite_ref-BBCrevamp_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCrevamp-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> Further improvements and expansion plans have been proposed. In December 2014, a <a href="/wiki/Transport_and_Works_Act_1992" title="Transport and Works Act 1992">Transport and Works Act</a> application was submitted for the construction of two through platforms as part of the <i>Manchester Piccadilly and Manchester Oxford Road Capacity Scheme</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> As of 2019, this application has not been approved by the incumbent government.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> To allow the station to accommodate high speed services under <a href="/wiki/High_Speed_2" title="High Speed 2">High Speed 2</a> proposals, five platforms would be required and the Metrolink station would be reconfigured. A preferred option of the more speculative <a href="/wiki/High_Speed_3" class="mw-redirect" title="High Speed 3">High Speed 3</a> programme requires the construction of more platforms underneath the existing platforms.
</p>
