<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manchester_Piccadilly_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Origins">Origins</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manchester_Piccadilly_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Origins">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Manchester_RJD_47.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Manchester_RJD_47.JPG/220px-Manchester_RJD_47.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Manchester_RJD_47.JPG/330px-Manchester_RJD_47.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Manchester_RJD_47.JPG/440px-Manchester_RJD_47.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2861" data-file-height="1916" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Manchester_RJD_47.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A 1910 <a href="/wiki/Railway_Clearing_House" title="Railway Clearing House">Railway Clearing House</a> Junction Diagram showing railways in Manchester</div></div></div>
<p>In June 1840, the <a href="/wiki/Manchester_and_Birmingham_Railway" title="Manchester and Birmingham Railway">Manchester and Birmingham Railway</a> (M&amp;BR) opened a temporary terminus on its line to <a href="/wiki/Stockport_railway_station" title="Stockport railway station">Stockport</a> on Travis Street. A large site, 1,700&#160;ft (518&#160;m) long by 500&#160;ft (152&#160;m) wide, was cleared of terraced houses and industrial premises to make way for the permanent station <i>Store Street</i> which was built on top of a viaduct, 30&#160;ft (9&#160;m) above ground level. The station was opened adjacent to London Road on 8 May 1842. It had two platforms, offices and passenger amenities and by then the line had been extended to <a href="/wiki/Crewe" title="Crewe">Crewe</a>. <sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHooper19953_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHooper19953-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-archive_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-archive-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Store Street was designed by M&amp;BR's chief engineer, <a href="/wiki/George_W._Buck" title="George W. Buck">George W. Buck</a>, who designed many of the line's structures including the <a href="/wiki/Stockport_Viaduct" title="Stockport Viaduct">Stockport Viaduct</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-eng_time_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eng_time-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Charles_Hutton_Gregory" title="Charles Hutton Gregory">Charles Hutton Gregory</a> was the assistant engineer. The station was shared from the beginning with the <a href="/wiki/Sheffield,_Ashton-under-Lyne_and_Manchester_Railway" title="Sheffield, Ashton-under-Lyne and Manchester Railway">Sheffield, Ashton-under-Lyne and Manchester Railway</a> (SA&amp;MR) following an agreement made by the promoters in 1837.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHooper19953_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHooper19953-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The M&amp;BR amalgamated with other railway companies to create the <a href="/wiki/London_and_North_Western_Railway" title="London and North Western Railway">London and North Western Railway</a> (LNWR) in 1846. The SA&amp;MR changed its name to the <a href="/wiki/Manchester,_Sheffield_and_Lincolnshire_Railway" title="Manchester, Sheffield and Lincolnshire Railway">Manchester, Sheffield and Lincolnshire Railway</a> (MS&amp;LR) three years later.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHooper19954_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHooper19954-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Manchester_London_Road">Manchester London Road</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manchester_Piccadilly_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Manchester London Road">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1847, the station was renamed <i>London Road</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-eng_time_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eng_time-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> In 1849 the <a href="/wiki/Manchester,_South_Junction_and_Altrincham_Railway" title="Manchester, South Junction and Altrincham Railway">Manchester, South Junction and Altrincham Railway</a> (MSJA&amp;R) began using the station after its line from <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Oxford_Road_railway_station" title="Manchester Oxford Road railway station">Manchester Oxford Road</a> was extended. Its single platform which opened on 1 August 1849 to the south of, and adjacent to the main part of station, was the predecessor of through platforms 13 and 14. The MSJA&amp;R's line connected to the main line south of the station and formed a through route to the LNWR's <a href="/wiki/Liverpool%E2%80%93Manchester_lines" title="Liverpool–Manchester lines">line to Liverpool</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-archive_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-archive-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHooper19954-5_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHooper19954-5-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Manchester_London_Road_stn,_old_postcard.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Manchester_London_Road_stn%2C_old_postcard.JPG/220px-Manchester_London_Road_stn%2C_old_postcard.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="138" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Manchester_London_Road_stn%2C_old_postcard.JPG/330px-Manchester_London_Road_stn%2C_old_postcard.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Manchester_London_Road_stn%2C_old_postcard.JPG/440px-Manchester_London_Road_stn%2C_old_postcard.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1614" data-file-height="1014" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Manchester_London_Road_stn,_old_postcard.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The frontage of London Road station <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;">&#8201;1905</span>, the main building dated from 1866.</div></div></div>
<p>By the 1850s, London Road was overcrowded and the relationship between the LNWR and MS&amp;LR had deteriorated. In 1862, the station was rebuilt and expanded so that it could be divided; the MS&amp;LR occupying the north-eastern side and the LNWR the south-western side. The station was given a new entrance building and concourse with each company having separate booking offices and passenger facilities. A 656&#160;ft (200&#160;m) long iron and glass <a href="/wiki/Trainshed" class="mw-redirect" title="Trainshed">trainshed</a> was built over the terminal platforms; it had two 95&#160;ft (29&#160;m) wide arched spans, one covering the LNWR platforms and the other the MS&amp;LR platforms.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHooper19955-6_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHooper19955-6-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> On 20 January 1866, a fatal accident occurred during the roof's construction, when part of it collapsed killing two workmen and injuring 30 others. The enquiry determined that the collapse was caused by strong winds and heavy snowfall. At the same time, both companies built <a href="/wiki/Warehouse" title="Warehouse">warehouses</a> around the northern side of the station, and the viaduct south of the station to <a href="/wiki/Ardwick" title="Ardwick">Ardwick</a> was widened to carry four tracks.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHooper19955-6_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHooper19955-6-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Manchester_Piccadilly_railway_station_from_the_footbridge.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Manchester_Piccadilly_railway_station_from_the_footbridge.jpg/220px-Manchester_Piccadilly_railway_station_from_the_footbridge.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Manchester_Piccadilly_railway_station_from_the_footbridge.jpg/330px-Manchester_Piccadilly_railway_station_from_the_footbridge.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Manchester_Piccadilly_railway_station_from_the_footbridge.jpg/440px-Manchester_Piccadilly_railway_station_from_the_footbridge.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Manchester_Piccadilly_railway_station_from_the_footbridge.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Interior of the Victorian train shed.</div></div></div>
<p>Within ten years, the station was again over-crowded as traffic continued to increase and expansion was again required. Between 1880 and 1883, the LNWR widened its side of the station and built more platforms, which were covered by two more 69&#160;ft (21&#160;m) wide arched spans to the trainshed. At the same time, the MSJ&amp;AR platform was taken out and rebuilt as an island platform on a girder bridge over Fairfield Street and linked to the main station by a footbridge. In May 1882, the improvements were opened.<sup id="cite_ref-archive_9-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-archive-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHooper19958_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHooper19958-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1897, the MS&amp;LR changed its name to the <a href="/wiki/Great_Central_Railway" title="Great Central Railway">Great Central Railway</a> (GCR); it opened a <a href="/wiki/Great_Central_Main_Line" title="Great Central Main Line">direct route</a> from the station to London in 1899.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHooper19958_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHooper19958-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1910, the adjacent <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Mayfield_railway_station" title="Manchester Mayfield railway station">Mayfield station</a> opened with four platforms to alleviate overcrowding at London Road. The stations were linked by a footbridge.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHooper19958_14-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHooper19958-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> Mayfield station closed to passengers in 1960 and to all traffic in 1986. The derelict station has remained in situ despite proposed redevelopment schemes including reopening it to relieve demand.<sup id="cite_ref-RailPR_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RailPR-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Following the <a href="/wiki/Railways_Act_1921" title="Railways Act 1921">1923 railway grouping</a>, the LNWR amalgamated with several other railway companies to create the <a href="/wiki/London,_Midland_and_Scottish_Railway" title="London, Midland and Scottish Railway">London, Midland and Scottish Railway</a> (LMS), and the GCR amalgamated with other railways to create the <a href="/wiki/London_and_North_Eastern_Railway" title="London and North Eastern Railway">London and North Eastern Railway</a> (LNER).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHooper199512_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHooper199512-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> The division of the station was maintained and it continued to be operated as two separate stations even after the <a href="/wiki/Nationalisation_of_British_Railways" class="mw-redirect" title="Nationalisation of British Railways">nationalisation of the railways</a> in 1948: One side was used by the <a href="/wiki/London_Midland_Region_of_British_Railways" title="London Midland Region of British Railways">London Midland Region of British Railways</a>, and the other by <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Region_of_British_Railways" title="Eastern Region of British Railways">Eastern Region</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-archive_9-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-archive-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Manchester_Piccadilly">Manchester Piccadilly</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manchester_Piccadilly_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Manchester Piccadilly">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Manchester_London_Road_Station_geograph-3004472-by-Ben-Brooksbank.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Manchester_London_Road_Station_geograph-3004472-by-Ben-Brooksbank.jpg/220px-Manchester_London_Road_Station_geograph-3004472-by-Ben-Brooksbank.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="172" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Manchester_London_Road_Station_geograph-3004472-by-Ben-Brooksbank.jpg/330px-Manchester_London_Road_Station_geograph-3004472-by-Ben-Brooksbank.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Manchester_London_Road_Station_geograph-3004472-by-Ben-Brooksbank.jpg/440px-Manchester_London_Road_Station_geograph-3004472-by-Ben-Brooksbank.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1852" data-file-height="1449" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Manchester_London_Road_Station_geograph-3004472-by-Ben-Brooksbank.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Construction of platforms 13 and 14 in 1959. Upon opening the station was renamed Piccadilly.</div></div></div>
<p>Between 1958 and 1966, London Road was rebuilt in the <a href="/wiki/West_Coast_Main_Line#Modernisation_by_British_Rail" title="West Coast Main Line">West Coast Main Line modernisation programme</a> undertaken by <a href="/wiki/British_Rail" title="British Rail">British Railways</a>. It was renamed "Manchester Piccadilly" on 12 September 1960.<sup id="cite_ref-archive_9-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-archive-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Manchester_Picadilly_1989_827033.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Manchester_Picadilly_1989_827033.jpg/220px-Manchester_Picadilly_1989_827033.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="159" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Manchester_Picadilly_1989_827033.jpg/330px-Manchester_Picadilly_1989_827033.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Manchester_Picadilly_1989_827033.jpg/440px-Manchester_Picadilly_1989_827033.jpg 2x" data-file-width="764" data-file-height="553" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Manchester_Picadilly_1989_827033.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Piccadilly station in 1989, with the concourse building opened in 1966, this was later redeveloped in 2002.</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/London_Midland_Region" class="mw-redirect" title="London Midland Region">London Midland Region</a> rebuilt the station at a cost of £1.75 million (equivalent to £40,200,000 in 2019 prices<sup id="cite_ref-inflation-UK_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-inflation-UK-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>) in preparation for electric train services to London. Most of the station was rebuilt, except for the Victorian trainsheds which remained mostly unaltered, although the two 1880's spans were shortened towards the concourse end. The station’s reconstruction took place in two phases, 1958–60 and 1963–66, the break was the result of a national credit squeeze restricting funding for railway modernisation.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHooper199513-16_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHooper199513-16-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The former MSJA&amp;R through platforms and bridges over Fairfield Street were rebuilt on a pre-stressed concrete slab bridge with cantilevered sides for the tracks. The layout in the trainshed was reconfigured to add several platforms. A new concourse and entrance was built, alongside which was a ten-storey office block which housed British Rail staff.<sup id="cite_ref-eng_time_10-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eng_time-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> On 11 May 1966, work was completed for the introduction of electric expresses to London.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHooper199513-16_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHooper199513-16-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHooper199553-64_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHooper199553-64-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The approach to the station was also redeveloped. The LNWR goods warehouse alongside the station approach closed in 1965 and a curved office block, <a href="/wiki/Gateway_House,_Manchester" title="Gateway House, Manchester">Gateway House</a> was opened in its place in 1969.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHooper199513-16_18-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHooper199513-16-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-eng_time_10-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eng_time-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> 
</p><p>Piccadilly remained open throughout the reconstruction, but disruption was experienced and extensive use was made of <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Mayfield_railway_station" title="Manchester Mayfield railway station">Manchester Mayfield</a> and <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Central_railway_station" title="Manchester Central railway station">Manchester Central</a> stations by diverted trains. When the work was completed, these stations were no longer required, and were closed and their services were diverted into Piccadilly.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHooper199513-16_18-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHooper199513-16-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Picc-Vic_tunnel_and_Metrolink">Picc-Vic tunnel and Metrolink</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manchester_Piccadilly_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Picc-Vic tunnel and Metrolink">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In the early 1970s, an underground station,<i>Piccadilly Low Level</i> was proposed as part of the <a href="/wiki/Picc-Vic_tunnel" title="Picc-Vic tunnel">Picc-Vic tunnel</a> project.<sup id="cite_ref-piccvic-leaflet_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-piccvic-leaflet-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> This scheme proposed creating a direct rail link between Piccadilly and <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Victoria_station" title="Manchester Victoria station">Manchester Victoria</a>, by building a tunnel and several underground stations under <a href="/wiki/Manchester_city_centre" title="Manchester city centre">Manchester city centre</a>. The project was cancelled in the late 1970s because of the high cost, and transport planners turned instead towards <a href="/wiki/Light_rail" title="Light rail">light rail</a> as a lower-cost option. This resulted eventually in the <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Metrolink" title="Manchester Metrolink">Manchester Metrolink</a> system which opened in the early 1990s linking the two stations by a street-level <a href="/wiki/Tram" title="Tram">tramway</a> and linking two converted rail lines to <a href="/wiki/Altrincham_Line" title="Altrincham Line">Altrincham</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bury_Line" title="Bury Line">Bury</a>. The <a href="#Piccadilly_tram_stop">tram stop</a> in the station's undercroft opened in 1992.<sup id="cite_ref-archive_9-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-archive-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-RailPR_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RailPR-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Windsor_Link">Windsor Link</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manchester_Piccadilly_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Windsor Link">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Between 1988 and 1989, Piccadilly's through platforms 13 and 14 were further lengthened.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> This work was performed in conjunction with the opening of the <a href="/wiki/Windsor_Link_Line,_Manchester" class="mw-redirect" title="Windsor Link Line, Manchester">Windsor Link</a> chord in <a href="/wiki/Salford,_Greater_Manchester" class="mw-redirect" title="Salford, Greater Manchester">Salford</a>, which allowed trains from destinations to the north of Manchester, such as <a href="/wiki/Bolton_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Bolton railway station">Bolton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Preston_railway_station" title="Preston railway station">Preston</a>, <a href="/wiki/Blackpool_North_railway_station" title="Blackpool North railway station">Blackpool</a> and Scotland, to run directly into Piccadilly via the through platforms and continue south to destinations such as <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Airport_station" title="Manchester Airport station">Manchester Airport</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stockport_railway_station" title="Stockport railway station">Stockport</a> and <a href="/wiki/Buxton_railway_station" title="Buxton railway station">Buxton</a>. Once completed, it allowed for many services from the north to be diverted from <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Victoria_station" title="Manchester Victoria station">Manchester Victoria</a>, which was reduced in size, and enhanced Piccadilly's status as Manchester's main station. In 1988, the link was opened; it was declared to be fully operational during the following year.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-HNWR_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HNWR-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2002_redevelopment">2002 redevelopment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manchester_Piccadilly_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 2002 redevelopment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Manchester_Piccadilly_station_approach_-_April_11_2005.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Manchester_Piccadilly_station_approach_-_April_11_2005.jpg/220px-Manchester_Piccadilly_station_approach_-_April_11_2005.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Manchester_Piccadilly_station_approach_-_April_11_2005.jpg/330px-Manchester_Piccadilly_station_approach_-_April_11_2005.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Manchester_Piccadilly_station_approach_-_April_11_2005.jpg/440px-Manchester_Piccadilly_station_approach_-_April_11_2005.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Manchester_Piccadilly_station_approach_-_April_11_2005.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The post-2002 main entrance to the station</div></div></div>
<p>Between 1998 and 2002, in preparation for the <a href="/wiki/2002_Commonwealth_Games" title="2002 Commonwealth Games">2002 Commonwealth Games</a>, the station underwent a £100 million redevelopment. The glass roof of the trainshed, which is a <a href="/wiki/Listed_building" title="Listed building">Grade II listed structure</a><sup id="cite_ref-NHLE_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NHLE-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> was re-glazed and re-painted. A new main entrance and enlarged concourse with a <a href="/wiki/Mezzanine" title="Mezzanine">mezzanine</a> level, designed by <a href="/wiki/Building_Design_Partnership" class="mw-redirect" title="Building Design Partnership">BDP</a>, replaced the 1960s structure, which had become insufficient for the number of passengers regularly using the station. A <a href="/wiki/Moving_walkway" title="Moving walkway">moving walkway</a> was installed to take passengers from the concourse to platforms 13 and 14 at the far south end of the station, which had previously necessitated a long walk. Another entrance was also created on Fairfield Street, which provides access to a new taxi rank along with a drop-off point for private cars.<sup id="cite_ref-RailPR_15-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RailPR-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-archive_9-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-archive-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BBCrevamp_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCrevamp-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Electrification">Electrification</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manchester_Piccadilly_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Electrification">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The station is unusual in having seen two different systems of <a href="/wiki/Railway_electrification_in_Great_Britain" title="Railway electrification in Great Britain">railway electrification</a>: The first electrified line into London Road was the <a href="/wiki/Manchester,_South_Junction_and_Altrincham_Railway" title="Manchester, South Junction and Altrincham Railway">MSJA&amp;R</a> line to <a href="/wiki/Altrincham_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Altrincham railway station">Altrincham</a>, a busy commuter route. It was electrified with overhead lines, energised at <a href="/wiki/Railway_electrification_in_Great_Britain#1,500_V_DC,_overhead_(historic)" title="Railway electrification in Great Britain">1,500 V DC</a> in 1931. London Road was the terminus of the electrification scheme which ran through to the through platforms.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHooper199512_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHooper199512-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The second line to be electrified using 1,500 V DC was the LNER's <a href="/wiki/Woodhead_Route" class="mw-redirect" title="Woodhead Route">Woodhead Route</a> from Manchester to Sheffield. Work on the scheme commenced in the late 1930s, but was stopped due to the <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">Second World War</a>, before being restarted in the early 1950s. Electrification was completed in September 1954.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHooper199513_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHooper199513-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> The two electric 1,500 V DC lines ran into different parts of the station.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/25_KV_AC_railway_electrification" class="mw-redirect" title="25 KV AC railway electrification">25 kV AC overhead</a> electrification, adopted as the national standard by British Railways, was brought to London Road/Piccadilly in the <a href="/wiki/West_Coast_Main_Line" title="West Coast Main Line">West Coast Main Line</a> electrification scheme starting in the late-1950s. The main line was electrified to <a href="/wiki/Crewe_railway_station" title="Crewe railway station">Crewe</a> by 1960 and London by 1966. At the same time, the 1,500 V electrification on the Altrincham line was cut back to <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Oxford_Road_railway_station" title="Manchester Oxford Road railway station">Oxford Road</a> to where the new system was extended from the south.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHooper199516_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHooper199516-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> The Altrincham line was converted to 25 kV in 1971.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The two systems co-existed for a number of years. The Woodhead Route was closed as a through line in 1981, but local services to <a href="/wiki/Glossop_Line" class="mw-redirect" title="Glossop Line">Glossop and Hadfield</a> continued to be operated by 1,500 V trains until the line was converted to 25 kV during 1984.<sup id="cite_ref-RCTSLNER10B_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RCTSLNER10B-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>During the 2010s, the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Hub" title="Northern Hub">Northern Hub</a> scheme saw electrification extended from <a href="/wiki/Liverpool-Manchester_lines" class="mw-redirect" title="Liverpool-Manchester lines">Manchester to Liverpool</a> in 2015,<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>  and <a href="/wiki/Manchester_to_Preston_Line" class="mw-redirect" title="Manchester to Preston Line">Manchester to Preston</a> and through to <a href="/wiki/Blackpool_branch_lines" title="Blackpool branch lines">Blackpool</a> in 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Architecture">Architecture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manchester_Piccadilly_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Architecture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Manchester_Picadilly_Station_Panorama.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Manchester_Picadilly_Station_Panorama.jpg/220px-Manchester_Picadilly_Station_Panorama.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="108" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Manchester_Picadilly_Station_Panorama.jpg/330px-Manchester_Picadilly_Station_Panorama.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Manchester_Picadilly_Station_Panorama.jpg/440px-Manchester_Picadilly_Station_Panorama.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6772" data-file-height="3312" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Manchester_Picadilly_Station_Panorama.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>One of the train shed's four arched roofs from the 1860s and 1880s.</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Listed_building" title="Listed building">listed</a> <a href="/wiki/Train_shed" title="Train shed">train shed</a> roof which is 105 metres wide between platforms 1 and 12, comprises four spans; two of the spans, 185 metres in length, were built over the eastern part of the station during the 1860s while the other two, at the western side measuring 150 metres, were constructed in the early 1880s. The roof is supported by masonry walls at the outer edges, which have round-headed windows alongside platforms 1 and 12, and rows of <a href="/wiki/Cast_iron" title="Cast iron">cast iron</a> <a href="/wiki/Column" title="Column">columns</a> along the platforms in its interior space. The roof spans have an arrangement of <a href="/wiki/Wrought_iron" title="Wrought iron">wrought iron</a> <a href="/wiki/Truss" title="Truss">trusses</a> with supporting cast iron <a href="/wiki/Strut" title="Strut">struts</a> on <a href="/wiki/Girder" title="Girder">girders</a>, which are evenly spaced between the columns.<sup id="cite_ref-NHLE_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NHLE-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As built, the roof was largely covered with <a href="/wiki/Slate" title="Slate">slates</a> with some areas of <a href="/wiki/Architectural_glass" title="Architectural glass">glazing</a>; over time, the slates were  replaced with boarded felt. Between 1997 and 1999, the station roof was refurbished and the traditional <a href="/wiki/Cladding_(construction)" title="Cladding (construction)">cladding</a> was replaced with around 10,000 panes of toughened glass that 'float' above the wrought iron trusses. Layers of nets have been installed, to catch falling glass in the event of any of the panes were to break.<sup id="cite_ref-eng_time_10-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eng_time-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Below the train shed is the undercroft that was used as a goods station. Cast iron columns and brick arches support the terminal platforms directly above. Since the early 1990s, the undercroft accommodates the Metrolink station, its tracks, <a href="/wiki/Siding" title="Siding">sidings</a>, and car parking.<sup id="cite_ref-eng_time_10-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eng_time-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> Before it was reused for the Metrolink, the cast-iron columns throughout the undercroft were encased in concrete as a protective measure against collision.<sup id="cite_ref-eng_time_10-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eng_time-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/George_W._Buck" title="George W. Buck">George W. Buck</a> designed the original <a href="/wiki/Skew_arch" title="Skew arch">skew arch</a> bridge over Fairfield Street; it had ten cast iron arch ribs, which formed one part of the brick arch viaduct, and was topped with open stonework <a href="/wiki/Parapet" title="Parapet">parapets</a>. The bridge was subsequently widened and wrought iron plate girders and transverse girders were added to support longitudinal joists with iron arch plates. In the 1960s, in the reconstruction programme, the cast iron arches and <a href="/wiki/Spandrel" title="Spandrel">spandrels</a> were  encased in concrete.<sup id="cite_ref-FSB_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FSB-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-eng_time_10-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eng_time-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> Platforms 13 and 14 are situated on top of this bridge.
</p><p>Many of the original station buildings were demolished during the 1960s to clear the way for a new approach.<sup id="cite_ref-eng_time_10-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eng_time-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> The main entrance leads to a concourse with ground floor, and since the 2000s, <a href="/wiki/Mezzanine" title="Mezzanine">mezzanine</a> levels. The Fairfield Street entrance leads to the Metrolink station in the undercroft and is linked to the rail platforms by escalators. Between 1997 and 2002, a redevelopment programme revised the station's layout and a glass partition wall with ticket barriers separating the concourse from the platforms was constructed.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> The station's approach leading to the end of Piccadilly was constructed in 1969 along with the "wavy" fronted <a href="/wiki/Gateway_House,_Manchester" title="Gateway House, Manchester">Gateway House</a> designed by the architect <a href="/wiki/Richard_Seifert" title="Richard Seifert">Richard Seifert</a>.  Gateway House was modernised during 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-eng_time_10-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eng_time-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Facilities">Facilities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manchester_Piccadilly_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Facilities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Manchester_Piccadilly_station.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Manchester_Piccadilly_station.jpg/220px-Manchester_Piccadilly_station.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Manchester_Piccadilly_station.jpg/330px-Manchester_Piccadilly_station.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Manchester_Piccadilly_station.jpg/440px-Manchester_Piccadilly_station.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Manchester_Piccadilly_station.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Fairfield Street entrance, the platforms inside are level with the brown brickwork</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Manchester_Piccadilly_concourse_(1)_5.19.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Manchester_Piccadilly_concourse_%281%29_5.19.jpg/220px-Manchester_Piccadilly_concourse_%281%29_5.19.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Manchester_Piccadilly_concourse_%281%29_5.19.jpg/330px-Manchester_Piccadilly_concourse_%281%29_5.19.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Manchester_Piccadilly_concourse_%281%29_5.19.jpg/440px-Manchester_Piccadilly_concourse_%281%29_5.19.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5152" data-file-height="3864" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Manchester_Piccadilly_concourse_(1)_5.19.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Retail and refreshment outlets on the station concourse</div></div></div>
<p>The Fairfield Street entrance, at basement level, serves the car park, the taxi rank, and the Metrolink station. Above it at track level is a concourse into which the main entrance feeds, housing ticket offices, information points, seating, timetables, toilets, shops, and food and drink outlets. Above the concourse is a second level of food outlets and bars, and the <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Trains" title="Virgin Trains">Virgin Trains</a> First Class Lounge. On the main concourse, doorways in a large glass partition wall access platforms 1 to 12. A <a href="/wiki/Moving_walkway" title="Moving walkway">travelator</a> leads to the upper concourse linked by a footbridge, steps and lift to platforms 13 and 14. The island lounge contains retail outlets, toilets and a departure lounge. There are vending machines, waiting areas and snack bars on platforms 13 and 14.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>Manchester Piccadilly is accessible for disabled people and has escalators and lifts to all levels, wide-access doors and gates, <a href="/wiki/Braille" title="Braille">braille</a> signs, hearing loops and disabled toilet facilities.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>Cycle racks are available on Fairfield Street and the long-stay car park and next to the tower block at the station front. During March 2010, <a href="/wiki/Manchester_City_Council" title="Manchester City Council">Manchester City Council</a> and Network Rail unveiled plans for a 'Cycle Centre' to provide secure facilities and on-site maintenance and hire services. The station has a taxi rank, drop-off/pick-up point, and short- and long-stay car parks.<sup id="cite_ref-parking_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-parking-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> accessible from Fairfield Street.<sup id="cite_ref-parking_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-parking-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> The long-stay <a href="/wiki/Multi-storey_car_park" class="mw-redirect" title="Multi-storey car park">multi-storey car park</a> is at the rear of the station.
</p><p>Ticket barriers were installed in Autumn 2016 between platforms 3 and 7, following an application by Virgin Trains.<sup id="cite_ref-application_for_ticket_gatelines_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-application_for_ticket_gatelines-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> Ticket barriers were fitted on platforms 1-3 by TransPennine Express, Platforms 9-12 remain ungated but for most of the day are staffed with ticket inspectors.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Layout">Layout</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manchester_Piccadilly_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Layout">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Platform 1 is at the north end of the station and the through platforms 13 and 14 are at the south end. Of the terminus platforms, 1-4 are typically used by eastbound services to Marple, New Mills, <a href="/wiki/Rose_Hill_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Rose Hill railway station">Rose Hill</a> and Sheffield via the <a href="/wiki/Hope_Valley_Line" class="mw-redirect" title="Hope Valley Line">Hope Valley Line</a>, and services on the <a href="/wiki/Glossop_Line" class="mw-redirect" title="Glossop Line">Glossop Line</a>, platforms 5-9 are the longest and are used mainly by <a href="/wiki/Virgin_West_Coast" class="mw-redirect" title="Virgin West Coast">Virgin West Coast</a> and <a href="/wiki/CrossCountry" title="CrossCountry">CrossCountry</a> services, platforms 10-12 are considerably shorter than the others and are usually used to accommodate local trains to <a href="/wiki/Crewe_railway_station" title="Crewe railway station">Crewe</a> and <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Airport_station" title="Manchester Airport station">Manchester Airport</a>, plus <a href="/wiki/Mid-Cheshire_line" title="Mid-Cheshire line">Mid-Cheshire line</a>, <a href="/wiki/Buxton_Line" class="mw-redirect" title="Buxton Line">Buxton Line</a> and South Wales services; platform 12 is the shortest and can only accommodate three coaches.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> The main entrance and concourse are to the front of the terminal platforms and the taxi and car drop-off entrance is on the southern side on Fairfield Street. The <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Metrolink" title="Manchester Metrolink">Metrolink</a> tram line passes under the station through the undercroft. Its platforms are under the concourse and railway platforms. To the south of Piccadilly, on the opposite side of Fairfield Street, is the derelict <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Mayfield_railway_station" title="Manchester Mayfield railway station">Manchester Mayfield</a> station, which was closed for railway use during 1986.
</p>
<div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:552px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Manchester_Piccadilly_plan.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Manchester_Piccadilly_plan.png/550px-Manchester_Piccadilly_plan.png" decoding="async" width="550" height="312" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Manchester_Piccadilly_plan.png/825px-Manchester_Piccadilly_plan.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f0/Manchester_Piccadilly_plan.png 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="568" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Manchester_Piccadilly_plan.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Layout plan of Piccadilly station, and surrounding streets.</div></div></div></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Future_proposals">Future proposals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manchester_Piccadilly_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Future proposals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In 2009, the <a href="/wiki/Greater_Manchester_Integrated_Transport_Authority" title="Greater Manchester Integrated Transport Authority">Greater Manchester Integrated Transport Authority</a> advocated reopening the neighbouring derelict Mayfield station to  alleviate capacity problems but the proposal was not advanced; plans focused on increasing track capacity on the cross-city route between Piccadilly and Oxford Road stations were pursued.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Northern_Hub">Northern Hub</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manchester_Piccadilly_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Northern Hub">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>During the early 2010s, <a href="/wiki/Network_Rail" title="Network Rail">Network Rail</a> promoted its <a href="/wiki/Northern_Hub" title="Northern Hub">Northern Hub</a> plans, estimated to cost in excess of £560&#160;million to improve the heavily congested rail network on the approach into Manchester.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> A pair of through platforms would be constructed at Piccadilly and the station linked to Manchester Victoria via the <a href="/wiki/Ordsall_Chord" title="Ordsall Chord">Ordsall Chord</a>, cutting journey times on Trans-Pennine routes.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-northernhub_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-northernhub-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> The construction of the Ordsall Chord made it possible for trains from the airport to travel via platforms 13 and 14 and Oxford Road to Manchester Victoria and Leeds and via the <a href="/wiki/Calder_Valley_Line" class="mw-redirect" title="Calder Valley Line">Calder Valley Line</a> to <a href="/wiki/Bradford_Interchange_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Bradford Interchange railway station">Bradford Interchange</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Phase 2 aims to alleviate congestion at platforms 13 and 14 by constructing a parallel elevated island platform and allow the minimum time between trains to be decreased from four to three minutes, improving reliability. It will allow four more trains an hour to be timetabled to Oxford Road including a second freight to Trafford Park.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> Approval for the platforms, at an estimated cost of £200&#160;million, was announced during July 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The proposals would simplify train operations at Piccadilly, creating close associations between pairs of lines leading out of the station and particular platforms while requiring only a few crossing moves. Platforms 1 to 4 would be primarily used for services on the 'east' lines, to and from Marple, Glossop and Huddersfield; platforms 5 to 12 would be for services on the 'fast' lines, to and from Crewe and Stoke; through platforms 13 to 16 would be dedicated to services on the present 'slow' lines, to and from Manchester Airport and Hazel Grove.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In July 2013, Network Rail consulted on three options for the additional platforms at Piccadily, all of which would affect local roads and the Grade II listed Star and Garter public house.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Construction was originally due to begin in 2016, but the project has now been delayed indefinitely<sup id="cite_ref-platform_doubt_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-platform_doubt-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="High_Speed_2">High Speed 2</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manchester_Piccadilly_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: High Speed 2">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hs2-manchester-piccadilly.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Hs2-manchester-piccadilly.png/220px-Hs2-manchester-piccadilly.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="178" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Hs2-manchester-piccadilly.png/330px-Hs2-manchester-piccadilly.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Hs2-manchester-piccadilly.png/440px-Hs2-manchester-piccadilly.png 2x" data-file-width="776" data-file-height="628" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hs2-manchester-piccadilly.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of the proposed expansion of Piccadilly for the HS2 project</div></div></div>
<p>To accommodate <a href="/wiki/High_Speed_2" title="High Speed 2">High Speed 2</a> (HS2), an extension would require four platforms and a 7.5 miles (12.1&#160;km) tunnel under south Manchester to join the <a href="/wiki/West_Coast_Main_Line" title="West Coast Main Line">West Coast Main Line</a> at <a href="/wiki/Ardwick" title="Ardwick">Ardwick</a>. Journey times to <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Airport" title="Manchester Airport">Manchester Airport</a> would be reduced to 9 minutes from 18, <a href="/wiki/Birmingham" title="Birmingham">Birmingham</a> 41 minutes from 86 minutes and London 68 minutes from 128. Station upgrades could include enhanced Metrolink services, improved road access and car parking. The line is planned to be completed by 2032.<sup id="cite_ref-hs_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hs-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A major redevelopment of the station and surrounding area has been proposed to complement the HS2 proposals involving the construction of a canopy over the HS2 platforms, the creation of a new entrance, and office, retail and residential development. Designs indicate that the derelict Mayfield Station and the Gateway House office block will be demolished.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> The plans were approved by the Government in November 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="High_Speed_3">High Speed 3</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manchester_Piccadilly_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: High Speed 3">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/High_Speed_3" class="mw-redirect" title="High Speed 3">High Speed 3</a> proposals include the construction of new platforms under Piccadilly station and the proposed HS2 platforms. The 2016 "Manchester Piccadilly Options Assessment" by the National Infrastructure Commission stated: "Addition of Northern Powerhouse Rail and Station to the Manchester Piccadilly system will be the last step of the process of transforming the station in to [sic] a transport super hub. The NPR station and its construction will need to be considered throughout the design and implementation of the other station improvements which form the station concept but which are delivered earlier. The NPR station is proposed to stay underground on its way east as it passes through Manchester city. This provides opportunities and offers location and orientation alternatives. Staying under the existing Piccadilly station or positioning NPR under the HS2 station box will maximise interchange efficiencies and travel distances. The orientation will also dictate the number of vertical connection cores also referred to as “drums” and their locations. The drums will have the function to connect all levels of transport to one and other [sic] at critical junction points.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>During October 2017, according to a report to the Manchester City Council’s executive, of the various proposals submitted, the development of an underground station has been selected as the preferred option for accommodating the envisioned HS3 services, which are speculated to involve the running of up to eight trains per hour, as well as connecting services with the in-development HS2. The importance of directly integrating this underground facility with the existing Piccadilly Station has been emphasized as well; however, the report observes that the necessary financing for the programme is still lacking.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Services">Services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manchester_Piccadilly_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:BR_Class_175_Piccadilly_ghost_livery.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/BR_Class_175_Piccadilly_ghost_livery.jpg/220px-BR_Class_175_Piccadilly_ghost_livery.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/BR_Class_175_Piccadilly_ghost_livery.jpg/330px-BR_Class_175_Piccadilly_ghost_livery.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/BR_Class_175_Piccadilly_ghost_livery.jpg/440px-BR_Class_175_Piccadilly_ghost_livery.jpg 2x" data-file-width="696" data-file-height="393" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:BR_Class_175_Piccadilly_ghost_livery.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Arriva_Trains_Wales" title="Arriva Trains Wales">Arriva Trains Wales</a> <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_175" title="British Rail Class 175">Class 175</a> at Piccadilly</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Class_185_at_Manchester_Piccadilly.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Class_185_at_Manchester_Piccadilly.jpg/220px-Class_185_at_Manchester_Piccadilly.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Class_185_at_Manchester_Piccadilly.jpg/330px-Class_185_at_Manchester_Piccadilly.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Class_185_at_Manchester_Piccadilly.jpg/440px-Class_185_at_Manchester_Piccadilly.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="1836" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Class_185_at_Manchester_Piccadilly.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/TransPennine_Express" title="TransPennine Express">TransPennine Express</a> <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_185" title="British Rail Class 185">Class 185</a> at Piccadilly</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Virgin_Train_at_Manchester_Piccadilly.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Virgin_Train_at_Manchester_Piccadilly.jpg/220px-Virgin_Train_at_Manchester_Piccadilly.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Virgin_Train_at_Manchester_Piccadilly.jpg/330px-Virgin_Train_at_Manchester_Piccadilly.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Virgin_Train_at_Manchester_Piccadilly.jpg/440px-Virgin_Train_at_Manchester_Piccadilly.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3888" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Virgin_Train_at_Manchester_Piccadilly.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Virgin_Trains" title="Virgin Trains">Virgin Trains</a> <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_390" title="British Rail Class 390"><i>Pendolino</i></a> service at Piccadilly</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Class_323_-_Manchester_Piccadilly.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Class_323_-_Manchester_Piccadilly.jpg/220px-Class_323_-_Manchester_Piccadilly.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Class_323_-_Manchester_Piccadilly.jpg/330px-Class_323_-_Manchester_Piccadilly.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Class_323_-_Manchester_Piccadilly.jpg/440px-Class_323_-_Manchester_Piccadilly.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3888" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Class_323_-_Manchester_Piccadilly.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Northern_(train_operating_company)" title="Northern (train operating company)">Northern</a> <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_323" title="British Rail Class 323">Class 323</a> at Piccadilly</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:CrossCountry_Class_220_Voyager_at_Manchester_Piccadilly.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/CrossCountry_Class_220_Voyager_at_Manchester_Piccadilly.jpg/220px-CrossCountry_Class_220_Voyager_at_Manchester_Piccadilly.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/CrossCountry_Class_220_Voyager_at_Manchester_Piccadilly.jpg/330px-CrossCountry_Class_220_Voyager_at_Manchester_Piccadilly.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/CrossCountry_Class_220_Voyager_at_Manchester_Piccadilly.jpg/440px-CrossCountry_Class_220_Voyager_at_Manchester_Piccadilly.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:CrossCountry_Class_220_Voyager_at_Manchester_Piccadilly.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/CrossCountry" title="CrossCountry">CrossCountry</a> <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_220" title="British Rail Class 220"><i>Voyager</i></a> at Piccadilly</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:East_Midlands_Train_at_Manchester_Piccadilly.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/East_Midlands_Train_at_Manchester_Piccadilly.jpg/220px-East_Midlands_Train_at_Manchester_Piccadilly.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/East_Midlands_Train_at_Manchester_Piccadilly.jpg/330px-East_Midlands_Train_at_Manchester_Piccadilly.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/East_Midlands_Train_at_Manchester_Piccadilly.jpg/440px-East_Midlands_Train_at_Manchester_Piccadilly.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:East_Midlands_Train_at_Manchester_Piccadilly.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/East_Midlands_Trains" title="East Midlands Trains">East Midlands Trains</a> <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_158" title="British Rail Class 158"><i>Express Sprinter</i></a> at Piccadilly</div></div></div>
<p>The station has 12 terminus platforms for services terminating from locations to the south of Manchester, and two through platforms, 13 and 14. The platforms are split into A and B sections to allow more than one train to stand. The through platforms 13 and 14 are used by through services via <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Oxford_Road_railway_station" title="Manchester Oxford Road railway station">Manchester Oxford Road</a> to <a href="/wiki/North_Wales" title="North Wales">North Wales</a>, <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_Lime_Street_railway_station" title="Liverpool Lime Street railway station">Liverpool</a>, North West England, <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Central_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Glasgow Central railway station">Glasgow</a> and <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh_Waverley_railway_station" title="Edinburgh Waverley railway station">Edinburgh</a>, and through services from <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Airport_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Manchester Airport railway station">Manchester Airport</a>.
</p><p>Manchester Piccadilly is currently served by six <a href="/wiki/Train_operating_company" title="Train operating company">train operating companies</a>:
</p><p><b><a href="/wiki/Northern_(train_operating_company)" title="Northern (train operating company)">Northern</a></b>
</p>
<ul><li>Local train services to stations in the Manchester area, primarily to destinations south and east of the city in Cheshire or Derbyshire and beyond.  These include <a href="/wiki/Hadfield_railway_station" title="Hadfield railway station">Hadfield</a>, <a href="/wiki/Glossop_railway_station" title="Glossop railway station">Glossop</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marple_railway_station" title="Marple railway station">Marple</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rose_Hill_Marple_railway_station" title="Rose Hill Marple railway station">Rose Hill Marple</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Mills_Central_railway_station" title="New Mills Central railway station">New Mills Central</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Sheffield railway station">Sheffield</a> via New Mills Central, <a href="/wiki/Hazel_Grove_railway_station" title="Hazel Grove railway station">Hazel Grove</a>, <a href="/wiki/Buxton_railway_station" title="Buxton railway station">Buxton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Crewe_railway_station" title="Crewe railway station">Crewe</a> via <a href="/wiki/Stockport_railway_station" title="Stockport railway station">Stockport</a> or Manchester Airport, <a href="/wiki/Stoke-on-Trent_railway_station" title="Stoke-on-Trent railway station">Stoke-on-Trent</a> via <a href="/wiki/Macclesfield_railway_station" title="Macclesfield railway station">Macclesfield</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Chester_railway_station" title="Chester railway station">Chester</a> via <a href="/wiki/Altrincham_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Altrincham railway station">Altrincham</a> and <a href="/wiki/Northwich_railway_station" title="Northwich railway station">Northwich</a>.</li>
<li>Services operate to the north and west to Liverpool Lime Street via <a href="/wiki/St_Helens_Junction_railway_station" title="St Helens Junction railway station">St Helens Junction</a> or <a href="/wiki/Warrington_Central_railway_station" title="Warrington Central railway station">Warrington Central</a> , <a href="/wiki/Preston_railway_station" title="Preston railway station">Preston</a> via <a href="/wiki/Bolton_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Bolton railway station">Bolton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Southport_railway_station" title="Southport railway station">Southport</a> via <a href="/wiki/Wigan_Wallgate_railway_station" title="Wigan Wallgate railway station">Wigan Wallgate</a>. Since 1 April 2016, Northern also operate the hourly service between Manchester Airport and <a href="/wiki/Blackpool_North_railway_station" title="Blackpool North railway station">Blackpool North</a> that was formerly run by <a href="/wiki/TransPennine_Express" title="TransPennine Express">TransPennine Express</a> (along with a small number of through trains to <a href="/wiki/Barrow-in-Furness_railway_station" title="Barrow-in-Furness railway station">Barrow-in-Furness</a> and <a href="/wiki/Windermere_railway_station" title="Windermere railway station">Windermere</a> via <a href="/wiki/Lancaster_railway_station" title="Lancaster railway station">Lancaster</a>).</li></ul>
<p>These are operated by a variety of trains of <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_142" title="British Rail Class 142">Class 142</a> Pacers, <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_150" title="British Rail Class 150">Class 150</a> or <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_156" title="British Rail Class 156">Class 156</a> <a href="/wiki/Diesel_multiple_unit" title="Diesel multiple unit">DMUs</a> or <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_323" title="British Rail Class 323">Class 323</a> and <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_319" title="British Rail Class 319">Class 319</a> electric units.
</p><p><b><a href="/wiki/Transport_for_Wales_Rail" class="mw-redirect" title="Transport for Wales Rail">Transport for Wales</a></b>
</p>
<ul><li>Hourly services via Chester and the <a href="/wiki/North_Wales_Coast_Line" title="North Wales Coast Line">North Wales Coast Line</a> to <a href="/wiki/Llandudno_railway_station" title="Llandudno railway station">Llandudno</a>, calling at Manchester Oxford Road, Newton-le-Willows, Earlestown, Warrington Bank Quay, Runcorn East, Frodsham, Helsby, Chester, Shotton, Flint, Prestatyn, Rhyl, Abergele &amp; Pensarn, Colwyn Bay, Llandudno Junction and Deganwy. Two trains per day run to <a href="/wiki/Holyhead_railway_station" title="Holyhead railway station">Holyhead</a> on weekdays only and some evening terminate at Chester.  Certain services to/from North Wales have been extended to Manchester Airport since the May 2016 timetable change.</li>
<li>Hourly services operate via Crewe, <a href="/wiki/Shrewsbury_railway_station" title="Shrewsbury railway station">Shrewsbury</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Welsh_Marches_Line" class="mw-redirect" title="Welsh Marches Line">Welsh Marches Line</a> to <a href="/wiki/Cardiff_Central_railway_station" title="Cardiff Central railway station">Cardiff Central</a>, with services continuing to <a href="/wiki/Carmarthen_railway_station" title="Carmarthen railway station">Carmarthen</a> or <a href="/wiki/Milford_Haven_railway_station" title="Milford Haven railway station">Milford Haven</a>. There are once daily services to <a href="/wiki/Tenby_railway_station" title="Tenby railway station">Tenby</a> &amp; <a href="/wiki/Pembroke_Dock_railway_station" title="Pembroke Dock railway station">Pembroke Dock</a> and to <a href="/wiki/Fishguard_Harbour_railway_station" title="Fishguard Harbour railway station">Fishguard Harbour</a>.</li></ul>
<p>All services (except for the 10:30 departure) are booked for a <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_175" title="British Rail Class 175">Class 175 <i>Coradia</i></a> unit. <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_158" title="British Rail Class 158">Class 158 <i>Express Sprinter</i></a> and occasionally Class 150 <i>Sprinter</i> units are seen operating these services when 175s are not available. Two services on the North Wales Coast route are operated by <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Mark_3" title="British Rail Mark 3">Mark 3 carriages</a> hauled by a <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_67" title="British Rail Class 67">Class 67</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><b><a href="/wiki/CrossCountry" title="CrossCountry">CrossCountry</a></b>
</p>
<ul><li>Hourly services to <a href="/wiki/Bournemouth_railway_station" title="Bournemouth railway station">Bournemouth</a> call at Stockport, Macclesfield, Stoke-on-Trent, <a href="/wiki/Stafford_railway_station" title="Stafford railway station">Stafford</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wolverhampton_railway_station" title="Wolverhampton railway station">Wolverhampton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Birmingham_New_Street_railway_station" title="Birmingham New Street railway station">Birmingham New Street</a>, <a href="/wiki/Birmingham_International_railway_station" title="Birmingham International railway station">Birmingham International</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coventry_railway_station" title="Coventry railway station">Coventry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leamington_Spa_railway_station" title="Leamington Spa railway station">Leamington Spa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Banbury_railway_station" title="Banbury railway station">Banbury</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oxford_railway_station" title="Oxford railway station">Oxford</a>, <a href="/wiki/Reading_railway_station" title="Reading railway station">Reading</a>, <a href="/wiki/Basingstoke_railway_station" title="Basingstoke railway station">Basingstoke</a>, <a href="/wiki/Winchester_railway_station" title="Winchester railway station">Winchester</a>, <a href="/wiki/Southampton_Airport_Parkway_railway_station" title="Southampton Airport Parkway railway station">Southampton Airport Parkway</a>, <a href="/wiki/Southampton_Central_railway_station" title="Southampton Central railway station">Southampton Central</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Brockenhurst_railway_station" title="Brockenhurst railway station">Brockenhurst</a>.</li>
<li>Hourly services to <a href="/wiki/Bristol_Temple_Meads_railway_station" title="Bristol Temple Meads railway station">Bristol Temple Meads</a> call at Stockport, Macclesfield, Stoke-on-Trent, Wolverhampton, Birmingham New Street, <a href="/wiki/Cheltenham_Spa_railway_station" title="Cheltenham Spa railway station">Cheltenham Spa</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Bristol_Parkway_railway_station" title="Bristol Parkway railway station">Bristol Parkway</a>. Some services continue to <a href="/wiki/Exeter_St_Davids_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Exeter St Davids railway station">Exeter St Davids</a>, <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_railway_station" title="Plymouth railway station">Plymouth</a> or <a href="/wiki/Paignton_railway_station" title="Paignton railway station">Paignton</a>.</li></ul>
<p>All CrossCountry services are regularly operated by <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_220" title="British Rail Class 220">Class 220 <i>Voyager</i></a> and <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_221" title="British Rail Class 221">Class 221 <i>Super Voyager</i></a> units.
</p><p><b><a href="/wiki/East_Midlands_Railway" title="East Midlands Railway">East Midlands Railway</a></b>
</p>
<ul><li>An hourly service from Liverpool Lime Street via Piccadilly to Sheffield and <a href="/wiki/Nottingham_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Nottingham railway station">Nottingham</a>, with most trains continuing to <a href="/wiki/Norwich_railway_station" title="Norwich railway station">Norwich</a>. These services are operated by Class 158 <i>Express Sprinter</i> units.</li></ul>
<p><b><a href="/wiki/TransPennine_Express" title="TransPennine Express">TransPennine Express</a></b> operate services on three routes.
</p>
<ul><li>The <a href="/wiki/North_TransPennine" class="mw-redirect" title="North TransPennine">North TransPennine</a> route has a half-hourly service to <a href="/wiki/York_railway_station" title="York railway station">York</a> via <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Victoria_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Manchester Victoria railway station">Manchester Victoria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Huddersfield_railway_station" title="Huddersfield railway station">Huddersfield</a> and <a href="/wiki/Leeds_railway_station" title="Leeds railway station">Leeds</a>, with trains running through to either <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_railway_station" title="Newcastle railway station">Newcastle</a> or <a href="/wiki/Middlesbrough_railway_station" title="Middlesbrough railway station">Middlesbrough</a>. There is also an hourly train to <a href="/wiki/Hull_Paragon_Interchange" title="Hull Paragon Interchange">Hull</a> via Huddersfield and Leeds, and an hourly stopping service to Huddersfield. There are two trains to <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Airport_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Manchester Airport railway station">Manchester Airport</a> on the North route.</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/South_TransPennine" class="mw-redirect" title="South TransPennine">South TransPennine</a> route runs from Manchester Airport via Piccadilly to Sheffield and <a href="/wiki/Cleethorpes_railway_station" title="Cleethorpes railway station">Cleethorpes</a>, operating hourly.</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/TransPennine_North_West" class="mw-redirect" title="TransPennine North West">TransPennine North West</a> route has an hourly service to <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh_Waverley_railway_station" title="Edinburgh Waverley railway station">Edinburgh Waverley</a> or <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Central_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Glasgow Central railway station">Glasgow Central</a> via <a href="/wiki/Preston_railway_station" title="Preston railway station">Preston</a>. In the opposite direction, this continues to Manchester Airport.  These services to/from Scotland operated along the newly electrified route over Chat Moss and Wigan North Western when the service switched to electric traction in 2013, however from May 2019 these services have reverted to running via <a href="/wiki/Bolton_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Bolton railway station">Bolton</a>.</li></ul>
<p><a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_185" title="British Rail Class 185">Class 185 <i>Desiro</i></a> units operate most TransPennine Express services, with the exception of the Scottish services which are operated by <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_350" title="British Rail Class 350">Class 350 <i>Desiro</i></a> units. The Class 185s were supplemented on the Hull and Cleethorpes services by <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_170" title="British Rail Class 170">Class 170 <i>Turbostar</i></a> units until July 2016 (these have now been transferred to <a href="/wiki/Chiltern_Railways" title="Chiltern Railways">Chiltern Railways</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><b><a href="/wiki/Virgin_Trains" title="Virgin Trains">Virgin Trains</a></b>
</p>
<ul><li>Three trains per hour to <a href="/wiki/Euston_railway_station" title="Euston railway station">London Euston</a>, two via Stoke-on-Trent and one via Crewe as part of the <a href="/wiki/InterCity_West_Coast" title="InterCity West Coast">InterCity West Coast</a> franchise, operated with <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_390" title="British Rail Class 390">Class 390 <i>Pendolino</i></a> units.</li></ul>

<td class="RMr" colspan="2"><div class="RMsi"><i>to</i> &#32;<table cellspacing="0" cellpadding="0" style="font-size:90%;font-weight:inherit;color:inherit;background:transparent;margin-top:-2px;margin-bottom:-2px;display:inline-table;vertical-align:middle;text-align:inherit;font-style:italic;"><tbody><tr><td style="text-align:inherit;padding:0;line-height:.9;font-size:inherit"><a href="/wiki/East_Didsbury_tram_stop" title="East Didsbury tram stop">East Didsbury</a> and</td></tr><tr><td style="text-align:inherit;padding:0;line-height:.9;font-size:inherit"><a href="/wiki/Manchester_Airport_tram_stop" class="mw-redirect" title="Manchester Airport tram stop">Manchester Airport</a></td></tr></tbody></table>&#32;</div>
